ttwetmore 2012-02-06T12:42:51-08:00
Since the data is in a access file format, I assume that it is a custom-designed spreadsheet.

Any reasonably competent developer who understands the GEDCOM format could take the CSV-dump of the spreadsheet and convert it to GEDCOM. There may some clever CSV-to-text application generator out there that could be programmed to do the conversion, but I doubt it. It would likely have to be a small custom development job. There are packages around for all development languages that know how to parse and process CSV files. Thus the front end of the custom code is trivial. The backend would convert each line in the CSV dump to an INDI record, and would have to understand how families are treated in the CSV in order to get the FAM records and the links between the INDIs and FAMs done right. The kind of stuff I used to do in my sleep.
ttwetmore 2012-02-06T12:45:30-08:00
Whoops, Access is a database not a spreadsheet. Doesn't change the answer very much however. Would need a text dump of the database and then custom code to parse and convert it.

If each Access table could be dumped in CSV or similar form the custom conversion code would be about the same.
gthorud 2012-02-06T14:30:20-08:00

It can be used for structural conversion of the existing tables to something that would be exported to a CSV format, something that would be better tailored to the input requirements of a CSV to GEDCOM converter - if needed.

GEDCOM Extensions
Hi all!

Thanks,
-Stan
ttwetmore 2012-02-08T12:54:33-08:00
Ain't one.
stan_m 2012-02-08T13:35:51-08:00
Is that because a "BetterGEDCOM" is going to start from scratch with a different file format?
ttwetmore 2012-02-08T14:41:44-08:00
There is no way sanctioned, formal way to modify GEDCOM, other than the ability of vendors to add a few custom tags. The LDS, who created GEDCOM, provided no process to change it or add to it.

Better GEDCOM has undertaken no obligation, either to extend the GEDCOM syntax into a richer model, or to use a different file format.

Most of us, I believe, think of the final file format as a secondary issue, whereas the genealogical model is more primary. Once the model is established many different file formats could be used to hold instances of objects from the model.

The general consensus seems to be that that final file format will be XML, though there are some who would prefer other formats.
stan_m 2012-02-08T16:20:41-08:00
My question came about because I read Tamura Jone's blog post on the SourceTemplate Initiative
(http://www.tamurajones.net/TheSourceTemplatesInitiative.xhtml) :

"GEDCOM is still the de facto standard, but GEDCOM does not support citation templates. The SourceTemplate Initiative aims to work with the BetterGEDCOM project to create GEDCOM extensions for the SourceTemplate model."

I thought that if a standardized citation template for GEDCOM was being developed, then some mechanism was in place for using it amongst the various vendors.
ttwetmore 2012-02-08T17:38:56-08:00
I don't know what Tamura meant, so I won't presume to guess. Any extensions to GEDCOM are unofficial and positively affect only the vendor that adds them, which adversely affects everyone else.

GEDCOM does not support citation templates. True.

There is no agreement yet whether Better GEDCOM will have citation templates AS PART OF ITS MODEL and therefore allow template objects to occur in BG files, or whether Better GEDCOM will just define source records and citation elements (aka metadata) in such a way that makes citation templates EASY TO APPLY to the Better GEDCOM data. Templates define how to display or view citations, and most of us believe that BG data should only contain content and not stylistic information. Others believe that citation templates are an important part of a genealogical data model, and that we must therefore deal with all the added complications that come from including them in the model.
stan_m 2012-02-09T07:37:25-08:00
Tom, thanks for the clarification.

PHP OAuth 2.0 & API Bridge Library
To anyone who's interested:
I have modified an existing OAuth library to work with 3 of the major Genealogy website: FamilySearch, Geni, and MyHeritage. The code is based in PHP and can also work as a API bridge. You can find a working example here:

ttwetmore 2012-03-04T19:48:21-08:00
My concerns are basic. Transport of data between/among genealogy desk top systems and on-line servers is difficult and error prone because of lack of adequate standards. Two solutions suggest themselves:

1. Invent a new standard that encompasses the variations and promote it ‘til it is accepted and implemented by a critical mass of the industry.

2. Forget new standards and create a third party program that can convert data between any two systems as well as is theoretically possible.

B-GEDCOM and GEDCOM-X have set themselves the task of solving 1. AncestorSync has set themselves the task of solving 2. AncestorSync is progressing faster than B-GEDCOM, and can already sync data between many different system pairs. We may reach fait accompli on 2. before any solution to 1. occurs, which may make working on 1. moot.

The fact that GEDCOM-X comes from the LDS leads me to believe that if there ever were B-GEDCOM and GEDCOM-X standards in contention that the GEDCOM-X would win out, whether it were the better standard or not. The Microsoft effect.

I hold the unpopular opinion that B-GEDCOM has failed, because it did not organize the technical work necessary to develop any model proposals. I see the creation of FHISO as a response to this failure. But FHISO seems to me to be an overly top-heavy organization that will interpret its task as something grander than developing a relatively simple standard for genealogical data transport. I hope I am incorrect and that FHISO will turn the tide and reach success. However, when I read the following on the FHISO thread: There will be a need for those with skills in management, finance, law, fundraising, public relations, community outreach, education, scheduling, and who knows what else...Without a strong organisational 'staff', FHISO will have a difficult time acheiving the goal it has set for itself, I lost all hope for FHISO. This is where my comment about playing games with empire and organization building came from. That statement scares the bejeesus out of me.
Andy_Hatchett 2012-03-04T20:11:44-08:00
Tom,

Why should that statement scare you?

bamcphee 2012-03-04T20:20:27-08:00

ttwetmore 2012-03-05T03:21:22-08:00
Andy,

You believe high quality technical work requires the pre-condition of large, complex organizations. I believe high quality technical work is more likely to be successful with small groups of experts working with relative freedom. I agree that once high quality work has been accomplished, a complex organization is usually required to realize that work into changes that affect our lives. My main worry about FHISO is that by the time enough of its infrastructure is in place, and technical subcommittees have been formed, and enough time has passed that the technical subcommittees have accomplished the organizationally imposed red tape to bring results to tangible standards proposals, that so much time will have passed (two, three, four years) that the whole effort will have been supplanted by another solution. I could be wrong though.

I hope you realize that all my comments are based on my desire that B-GEDCOM succeed.

The fact that GEDCOM-X is being developed by a complex organization is not a compelling or even logical argument that a complex organization is required. If you ask the GEDCOM-X folk after they've had a few beers, they will tell you that their work is constrained by factors imposed by their complex organization. They are developing standards to accommodate the massive collection of digital records they already possess, not a standard to dictate how they will archive their massive collection of digital records. There is a large and not very subtle difference.
louiskessler 2012-03-05T08:52:53-08:00
Tom, et al.,

I for one, appreciate Tom's input into BetterGEDCOM. He's spent a lot of his time and effort contributing in the wiki, technologically and promotionally to it. I can see his frustration in that he (as we all) see a need for a new standard, but it has appeared to have been moving at a snail's pace.

I too have over the past year, tried to jumpstart BetterGEDCOM and get things happening and try to get the group to produce something.

But if you take a step back and look at the bigger picture, BetterGEDCOM has in fact been doing very important things.

It has been making the need for a new standard apparent.

It has got the big players to start thinking about it, whether they are in cooperation mode (FamilySearch) or not (Ancestry.com).

It has made everyone aware and has got everyone to start talking about it. All the writings in genealogy blogs have been about how poor data transfer is and that something needs to be done.

It has collected major knowledge about different genealogy standards, international standards, methods of recording and transferring data.

It has promoted citation standards and even organized work with AncestorSync for a project on SourceTemplates.

And the latest work to get official and get organized has probably been the most important step. Robert was working very hard to promote FHISO and BetterGEDCOM at RootsTech and he talked to some important players who were indeed listening.

I see progress being made on all fronts. I don't see GEDCOM X as being a competitor. They are working primarily to represent their own online family tree's data structure. I don't think theirs will necessarily rule (see: Ancestry.com, MyHeritage, AncestrySync and the many other APIs available), and there still will need to be an adjudicator to coordinate all of these.

I am very encouraged by all the progress made by the BetterGEDCOM folk (who are all volunteers spending their own free time) to actually get as far as they have and reached this point.

The written standard will come. The entire genealogy community is working towards it. And FHISO is getting ready to oversee that effort.

Andy_Hatchett 2012-03-20T18:59:37-07:00
The inactivity is easily explained.

Since January 1, 2012 there have only been 10 Wiki members that have initiated New posts.

While there have been responses to older posts there has been relatively little new material introduced and people get tired of re-hashing old stuff with no actual decisions being made.

The truth of the matter is that a Wiki provides for no actual decision making process except agreement among the parties involved.

Thus, until some sort of consensus is reached among the various members, there is no path for real advancement toward the Wiki's stated goal.

It seems to me there are two 'camps', those who want to 'fix" GEDCOM and those who want to 'replace' GEDCOM.

Perhaps it is time that those in each 'camp' start developing an actual model for their favored solution rather than continuing to discuss which ( fix or replace) should be undertaken.

Thoughts and comments welcomed.

Andy Hatchett
Moderator

rmburkhead 2012-03-03T13:26:33-08:00
Hi Tom,

You have raised some questions and concerns important to everyone interested in BetterGEDCOM, FHISO, and to anyone else interested in the state of standards development in the genealogy community. I am certain that you are not alone in asking these things, and I thank you for raising them here so that we can all discuss the issues openly.

Some of the questions you raised have been discussed in other forums, notably in the BetterGEDCOM Developer’s Meeting held weekly on Mondays. That you have raised these issues here tells me that we have failed to effectively communicate with the wider BetterGEDCOM community--specifically, with those who have limited their participation in BetterGEDCOM to the wiki and its discussion forums. On behalf of the DTO members, I apologize for this failure. As its Chair, I will try to ensure that we do a better job communicating through more channels from this point forward.

Let me share some things with you, Brett, Adrian and the BetterGEDCOM community, in order to help everyone understand where we are and where we are headed.

First, we have been promoting the concept of FHISO as a community-owned “home” for standards in the genealogy industry to key constituents. This began in earnest during RootsTech 2012, when the formation of FHISO was officially announced, and some key players in the vendor community were contacted individually. We are extremely pleased and encouraged with the responses we have received from some very influential companies and organizations. I anticipate that, in the near future, the fruits of these efforts will be announced. You can understand each organization’s desire to communicate directly to their own community.

We continue to be encouraged by the expressions of interest and support from other companies, organizations, professionals, and individuals. We anticipate broad support in the community, not only here in the US, but also across the globe. We are specifically making an effort to ensure that we bring the international community together toward our common purpose.

As you might expect, there are many moving parts that must be orchestrated in order to create a new organization. Some of these parts are governmental and/or legal, and they move at a pace that is out of our direct control. We are near the end of this part of the process, and will be able to share this news with everyone in short order. In addition to the mechanical process of bringing the organization into being, resources must be assembled and coordinated. We are at the point, now, and have identified several areas where others can contribute. It is our hope that the positive reaction we have had thus far will translate into volunteers and action.

You’ve asked specifically about “restarting the effort of developing the BetterGEDCOM standard”. In my mind, that process never stopped. Discussions have continued, much as they have. The DTO group was formed from within BetterGEDCOM as an acknowledgement that while valuable work was being done, and valuable information was being generated, we needed a discernible path to consensus and a process for synthesizing that work into a standard. FHISO’s intent is to define that path and that process.

We believe, with input from the community, that an innovative standardization process can be introduced. With the support of appropriate resources and technology that process can help us organize our efforts into teams, and we can then move forward together to address both the short-term and long-term standardization needs of the industry.

Your raising these concerns at this point in the process is timely. We are coming to a point in the initial mechanical effort to create this organization where things will start to move more quickly, and more participation will be needed. In some areas we will be asking for help immediately. In some other areas, there are still a few things to sort out and we thank everyone for their patience.

I would be happy to address any specific concerns or questions, to the extent that I am able. I can be contacted directly via email at rmburkhead *at* fhiso *dot* org.

Thanks,

Robert Burkhead
Chair, Family History Information Standards Organisation
GeneJ 2012-03-03T13:38:08-08:00
Greetings from the workroom,

FHISO is a standards-setting organization--it's both technical and non-technical folks working (long and hard) to make this a reality. Those of us on the DTO are (really, really) thankful for the mentoring and assistance being received--it's coming from within and beyond the BetterGEDCOM membership.

We could use more help, including technical assistance, in the work to

(a) build and/or arrange tools to support an extendable collaboration infrastructure and flow (working groups, project teams, technical standing committees, etc.). The tools must support a speedy process, and thus aid in a range of work flows (static, real-time and asynchronous).
(b) hands-on assistance to develop materials that seed an initial set of working groups and project teams. In support of same, some particular work with the BetterGEDCOM Requirements Catalog is needed.
(c) website design and development,
(d) writers/content creators and, as appropriate, translators,
(e) graphic design/promotional materials suitable for independent presentation to vendors, family historians and genealogical organizations around the globe,
(f) technical tools and other assistance supporting outreach,
(g) nonprofit accounting, membership and database infrastructure,
(h) legal support to finalize things like the privacy policy and terms of use ...

One community, one standard.
We've got to work together “for the common good.”[1] Let’s develop the potential of FHISO as a community-owned, standards-setting organization and realize the benefits.

If you can help, please contact us at fhiso *AT* fhiso *DOT* org. We thank you all for your continued support.

Bear back to the workroom--GeneJ

[1] Dr. Bill (William L.) Smith, “FHISO: One community, one standard--feels good to me; to you?” _Examiner.com_ (http://www.examiner.com/genealogy-in-springfield-mo/fhiso-one-community-one-standard-feels-good-to-me-to-you: published 1 March 2012)

GeneJ 2012-03-05T22:14:25-08:00
Changes coming to the BetterGEDCOM wiki
During the BetterGEDCOM Developers Meeting a week ago, those in attendance presented ideas for how the information on the wiki might be made more accessible and easier to overview. GeneJ was tasked with follow up on this topic, and further discussion took place during the Developers Meeting today (March 5).

A group of wiki members indicated their desire to advance the ideas. In addition to some wiki housekeeping, two specific

(1) The BetterGEDCOM Requirements Catalog represents a substantial body of work, but information about the requirements is often discussed in depth elsewhere on the wiki. An effort is being mobilized to (a) link/associate wiki pages and discussions back to the Requirements Catalog entries; (b) overviewing then the collective information related to a topic in the catalog. Note that minor modification of the Requirements Catalog template may be necessary in this process.

(2) From the work with the Requirements Catalog (1), make recommendations about requirements that are sufficiently independent of a core project to support working group-like activity.

I've established this discussion to solicit ideas/input from BetterGEDCOM members, and to provide a forum for those who attended today's meeting to follow up or expand on our discussions. --GJ

greglamberson 2012-04-21T11:10:34-07:00
Greetings Old Friends
It's been a long time since I have participated here, but after much water under the bridge, I am back involved with the effort to improve genealogical standards that we began here nearly a year and a half ago.

For those of you who might not know me, I was a founding member of BetterGEDCOM and contributed a great deal of time and energy to this effort. Subsequent difficulties caused me to leave the wiki and the effort, but now I have come back to be involved, as much as I am able, in this subject which is dear to me.
Specifically, members of FHISO have contacted me and asked if I would consider getting involved again. My schedule is pretty full these days, but I have agreed to work with FHISO to try to move forward in the genealogical technology standards realm in continuance of the work we were doing here back when I was active.
Basically I wanted to drop by and say hello and rekindle our association and hopefully our energy. So hello, everyone, and it's great to be back involved in this movement and this effort!
I look forward to renewing friendships and making progress in genealogical technology standards!

Regards,

Greg Lamberson

GeneJ 2012-06-04T13:59:47-07:00
Full wiki backup/download successful. TY Greg Lamberson
As many are aware, Wikispaces does not provide a full back up of the BetterGEDCOM wiki. We've known this for some time and several members have been working with other tools, trying to extract a full backup (pages, files, discussions) from the BetterGEDCOM wiki

Last week, Greg Lamberson took his hand to the challenge and got 'er done!

This means that we have been able to extract a file containing all the pages, histories, files _and_ discussions.

Having the information in form that makes it more accessible, thus more useful, requires a more advanced solution. Greg and others are working on a set of more advanced solutions now.

Will keep you posted.

Thank you, Greg Lamberson.

louiskessler 2012-09-07T20:40:27-07:00
Genealogy Q&A; Site
An attempt is underway to build up enough interest and momentum in the genealogy community to support a vendor-independent community-run Question and Answer site for Genealogy and Family History.

The site proposal area is at http://bit.ly/Pzv6rv

As I write this, there are 129 followers. The site will require at least 200 people to commit to helping get the questions and answers during a Beta test period that will last a minimum of 90 days. If sufficient traffic and interest is reached during the Beta, the site will be made permanent and become a great resource for all family researchers worldwide.

More info in my blog post at: http://www.beholdgenealogy.com/blog/?p=1128

This site would be a great complement to the work being done at BetterGEDCOM and by FHISO.

I encourage everybody to help out and sign up at: http://bit.ly/Pzv6rv

Louis
